        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The status of ambient temp. sodium ion batteries is reviewed in light of recent developments in anode, electrolyte and cathode materials.  These devices, although early in their stage of development, are promising for large-scale grid storage applications due to the abundance and very low cost of sodium-contg. precursors used to make the components.  The engineering knowledge developed recently for highly successful Li ion batteries can be leveraged to ensure rapid progress in this area, although different electrode materials and electrolytes will be required for dual intercalation systems based on sodium.  In particular, new anode materials need to be identified, since the graphite anode, commonly used in lithium systems, does not intercalate sodium to any appreciable extent.  A wider array of choices is available for cathodes, including high performance layered transition metal oxides and polyanionic compds.  Recent developments in electrodes are encouraging, but a great deal of research is necessary, particularly in new electrolytes, and the understanding of the SEI films.  The engineering modeling calcns. of Na-ion battery energy d. indicate that 210 Wh kg-1 in gravimetric energy is possible for Na-ion batteries compared to existing Li-ion technol. if a cathode capacity of 200 mAh g-1 and a 500 mAh g-1 anode can be discovered with an av. cell potential of 3.3 V.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref2" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1021/cr500192f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yabuuchi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahbi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research Development on Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Rev.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>114</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">11636</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">11682</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/cr500192f</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D114%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D11636-11682%26journal%3DChem.%2BRev.%26author%3DN.%2BYabuuchi%26author%3DK.%2BKubota%26author%3DM.%2BDahbi%26author%3DS.%2BKomaba%26title%3DResearch%2BDevelopment%2Bon%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fcr500192f&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11157&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fcr500192f&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review of sodium-ion battery technol.                         cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atomic Structure and Kinetics of NASICON NaxV2(PO4)3 Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jian, Zelang; Yuan, Chenchen; Han, Wenze; Lu, Xia; Gu, Lin; Xi, Xuekui; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Chen, Wen; Chen, Dongfeng; Ikuhara, Yuichi; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">24</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">27</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4265-4272</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)3 is one of the most important cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries, delivering about two Na extn./insertion from/into the unit structure.  To understand the mechanism of sodium storage, a detailed structure of rhombohedral Na3V2(PO4)3 and its sodium extd. phase of NaV2(PO4)3 are investigated at the at. scale using a variety of advanced techniques.  It is found that two different Na sites (6b, M1 and 18e, M2) with different coordination environments co-exist in Na3V2(PO4)3, whereas only one Na site (6b, M1) exists in NaV2(PO4)3.  When Na is extd. from Na3V2(PO4)3 to form NaV2(PO4)3, Na+ occupying the M2 site (CN = 8) is extd. and the rest of the Na remains at M1 site (CN = 6).  In addn., the Na atoms are not randomly distributed, possibly with an ordered arrangement in M2 sites locally for Na3V2(PO4)3.  Na+ ions at the M1 sites in Na3V2(PO4)3 tend to remain immobilized, suggesting a direct M2-to-M2 conduction pathway.  Only Na occupying the M2 sites can be extd., suggesting about two Na atoms are able to be extd. from the Na3V2(PO4)3 structure.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref4" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1039/c5ee01365h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nazar, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Talaie, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duffort, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Smith, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fultz, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structure of the High Voltage Phase of Layered P2-Na<sub>2/3-x</sub>[Mn<sub>1/2</sub>Fe<sub>1/2</sub>]O<sub>2</sub> and the Positive Effect of Ni Substitution on its Stability</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-ion mobility in layered Na2FePO4F and olivine Na[Fe,Mn]PO4</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tripathi, R.; Wood, S. M.; Islam, M. S.; Nazar, L. F.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2257-2264</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The Na-ion battery is currently the focus of much research interest due to its cost advantages and the relative abundance of sodium as compared to lithium.  Olivine NaMPO4 (M = Fe, Fe0.5Mn0.5, Mn) and layered Na2FePO4F are interesting materials that have been reported recently as attractive pos. electrodes.  Here, we report their Na-ion conduction behavior and intrinsic defect properties using atomistic simulation methods.  In the olivines, Na ion migration is essentially restricted to the [010] direction along a curved trajectory, similar to that of LiMPO4, but with a lower migration energy (0.3 eV).  However, Na/M antisite defects are also predicted to have a lower formation energy: the higher probability of tunnel occupation with a relatively immobile M2+ cation - along with a greater vol. change on redox cycling - contributes to the poor electrochem. performance of the Na-olivine.  Na+ ion conduction in Na2FePO4F is predicted to be two-dimensional (2D) in the interlayer plane with a similar low activation energy.  The antisite formation energy is slightly higher; furthermore, antisite occupation would not be predicted to impede transport significantly owing to the 2D pathway.  This factor, along with the much lower vol. change on redox cycling, is undoubtedly responsible for the better electrochem. performance of the layered structure.  Where vol. change and structural effects do not incur impediments, Na-ion materials may present significant advantages over their Li counterparts.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref6" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1038/nchem.2923"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Maitra, U.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">House, R.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Oxygen redox chemistry without excess alkali-metal ions in Na2/3[Mg0.28Mn0.72]O2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Maitra, Urmimala; House, Robert A.; Somerville, James W.; Tapia-Ruiz, Nuria; Lozano, Juan G.; Guerrini, Niccolo; Hao, Rong; Luo, Kun; Jin, Liyu; Perez-Osorio, Miguel A.; Massel, Felix; Pickup, David M.; Ramos, Silvia; Lu, Xingye; McNally, Daniel E.; Chadwick, Alan V.; Giustino, Feliciano; Schmitt, Thorsten; Duda, Laurent C.; Roberts, Matthew R.; Bruce, Peter G.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">288-295</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAHBB</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1755-4330</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Research</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The search for improved energy-storage materials has revealed Li- and Na-rich intercalation compds. as promising high-capacity cathodes.  They exhibit capacities in excess of what would be expected from alkali-ion removal/reinsertion and charge compensation by transition-metal (TM) ions.  The addnl. capacity is provided through charge compensation by oxygen redox chem. and some oxygen loss.  It has been reported previously that oxygen redox occurs in O 2p orbitals that interact with alkali ions in the TM and alkali-ion layers (i.e., oxygen redox occurs in compds. contg. Li+-O(2p)-Li+ interactions).  Na2/3[Mg0.28Mn0.72]O2 exhibits an excess capacity and here we show that this is caused by oxygen redox, even though Mg2+ resides in the TM layers rather than alkali-metal (AM) ions, which demonstrates that excess AM ions are not required to activate oxygen redox.  We also show that, unlike the alkali-rich compds., Na2/3[Mg0.28Mn0.72]O2 does not lose oxygen.  The extn. of alkali ions from the alkali and TM layers in the alkali-rich compds. results in severely underbonded oxygen, which promotes oxygen loss, whereas Mg2+ remains in Na2/3[Mg0.28Mn0.72]O2, which stabilizes oxygen.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref7" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702619"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Prussian Blue Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries and Other Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. K2Mn1-xCoxFe(CN)6 (x = 0, 0.05, 0.1 and 0.2) was selected as a cathode material for sodium ion batteries to increase their lattice parameters, along with the large available tunnels for Na+ diffusion.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium iron hexacyanoferrate (Fe-HCF) has been proposed as a promising cathode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) because of its desirable advantages, including high theor. capacity (∼170 mAh g-1), eco-friendliness, and low cost of worldwide rich sodium and iron resources.  Nonetheless, its application faces a no. of obstacles due to poor electronic cond. and structural instability.  In this work, Fe-HCF nanospheres (NSs) were first synthesized and fabricated by an in situ graphene rolls (GRs) wrapping method, forming a 1D tubular hierarchical structure of Fe-HCF NSs@GRs.  GRs not only provide fast electronic conduction path for Fe-HCF NSs but also effectively prevent org. electrolyte from reaching active materials and inhibit the occurrence of side reactions.  The Fe-HCF NSs@GRs composite has been used as a binder-free cathode with a capacity of ∼110 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 150 mA g-1 (∼1C), the capacity retention of ∼90% after 500 cycles.  Moreover, the Fe-HCF NSs@GRs cathode displays a super high rate capability with ∼95 mAh g-1 at 1500 mA g-1 (∼10C).  The results suggest that the 1D tubular structure of 2D GRs-wrapped Fe-HCF NSs is promising as a high-performance cathode for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref15" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.7b05178"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nie, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Le, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Prussian Blue Analogue with Fast Kinetics Through Electronic Coupling for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Through the inhibitor and temp. control, the border-rich structure was obtained, which provides a good contact between electrode-electrolyte interfaces and increases the transmission path for Na+ ions.  In addn., the as-prepd. sample with rhombohedral phase demonstrated lower band gap and lower energy barrier for Na+ ions insertion.  Benefiting from the kinetics optimization, the as-prepd. electrode exhibited initial capacity of 120 mA h g-1 and maintained nearly 80% after 280 cycles at c.d. of 100 mA g-1.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Prussian Blue Analogs for Rechargeable Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Baoqi; Han, Yu; Wang, Xiao; Bahlawane, Naoufal; Pan, Hongge; Yan, Mi; Jiang, Yinzhu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">iScience</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Non-lithium energy storage devices, esp. sodium ion batteries, are drawing attention due to insufficient and uneven distribution of lithium resources.  Prussian blue and its analogs (Prussian blue analogs [PBAs]), or hexacyanoferrates, are well-known since the 18th century and have been used for hydrogen storage, cancer therapy, biosensing, seawater desalination, and sewage treatment.  Owing to their unique features, PBAs are receiving increasing interest in the field of energy storage, such as their high theor. specific capacity, ease of synthesis, as well as low cost.  In this review, a general summary and evaluation of the applications of PBAs for rechargeable batteries are given.  After a brief review of the history of PBAs, their crystal structure, nomenclature, synthesis, and working principle in rechargeable batteries are discussed.  Then, previous works classified based on the combination of insertion cations and transition metals are analyzed comprehensively.  The review includes an outlook toward the further development of PBAs in electrochem. energy storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref22" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b04151"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Preparation of Prussian Blue Submicron Particles with a Pore Structure by Two-Step Optimization for Na-Ion Battery Cathodes</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Traditional Prussian blue (Fe4[Fe(CN)6]3) synthesized by simple rapid pptn. shows poor electrochem. performance because of the presence of vacancies occupied by coordinated water.  When the pptn. rate is reduced and polyvinylpyrrolidone K-30 is added as a surface active agent, the as-prepd. Prussian blue has fewer vacancies in the crystal structure than in that of traditional Prussian blue.  It has a well-defined face-centered-cubic structure, which can provide large channels for Na+ insertion/extn.  The material, synthesized by slow pptn., has an initial discharge capacity of 113 mA h g-1 and maintains 93 mA h g-1 under a c.d. of 50 mA g-1 after 150 charge-discharge cycles.  After further optimization by a chem. etching method, the complex nanoporous structure of Prussian blue has a high Brunauer-Emmett-Teller surface area and a stable structure to achieve high specific capacity and long cycle life.  Surprisingly, the electrode shows an initial discharge capacity of 115 mA h g-1 and a Coulombic efficiency of approx. 100% with capacity retention of 96% after 150 cycles.  Exptl. results show that Prussian blue can also be used as a cathode for Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref23" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1039/c5cc01180a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, X.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z.-F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Prussian Blue Without Coordinated Water as a Superior Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Crystallographic-plane tuned Prussian-blue wrapped with RGO: a high-capacity, long-life cathode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Hui; Wang, Li; Chen, Shuangming; Li, Guopeng; Quan, Junjie; Xu, Enze; Song, Li; Jiang, Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3569-3577</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Designing Prussian blue with optimally exposed crystal planes and confining it in a conductive matrix are crit. issues for improving its sodium storage performance, and will result in much improved sodium ion adsorption and diffusion, together with improved electron mobility.  Here, we firstly illustrate through DFT simulations that the {100} lattice planes and [100] direction of the KxFeFe(CN)6 crystal are the preferred occupation sites and diffusion route for sodium ions.  In addn., through coupling with RGO, KxFeFe(CN)6 electrodes exhibit better electronic cond.  Accordingly, {100} plane-capped cubic K0.33FeFe(CN)6 wrapped in RGO was fabricated using a facile CTAB-assisted method.  Due to the highly robust framework, higher sp. surface area, greatly reduced no. of lattice water defects and conductive RGO coating, K0.33FeFe(CN)6/RGO exhibits superior electrochem. performance in sodium-ion batteries.  As a cathode, the RGO-coated K0.33FeFe(CN)6 yields an initial discharge-charge capacity of 160 mA h g-1 at a rate of 0.5C, and an excellent capacity retention of 92.2% at 0.5C and 90.1% at 10C after 1000 and 500 cycles.  Furthermore, x-ray diffraction, DFT simulation, XANES and EXAFS verified that the structural changes during the Na-ion insertion-extn. processes are highly reversible.  All these results suggest that {100} plane-capped K0.33FeFe(CN)6/RGO has excellent potential as a cathode for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref26" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-014-0588-7"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">You, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nam, K.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.-G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium Iron Hexacyanoferrate With High Na Content as a Na-Rich Cathode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nano Res.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">117</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">128</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A review of the features and analyses of the solid electrolyte interphase in Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Verma, Pallavi; Maire, Pascal; Novak, Petr</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">55</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) is a protecting layer formed on the neg. electrode of Li-ion batteries as a result of electrolyte decompn., mainly during the 1st cycle.  Battery performance, irreversible charge loss, rate capability, cyclability, exfoliation of graphite and safety are highly dependent on the quality of the SEI.  Therefore, understanding the actual nature and compn. of SEI is of prime interest.  If the chem. of the SEI formation and the manner in which each component affects battery performance are understood, SEI could be tuned to improve battery performance.  In this paper key points related to the nature, formation, and features of the SEI formed on carbon neg. electrodes are discussed.  SEI was analyzed by various anal. techniques amongst which FTIR and XPS are most widely used.  FTIR and XPS data of SEI and its components as published by many research groups are compiled in tables for getting a global picture of what is known about the SEI.  This article shall serve as a handy ref. as well as a starting point for research related to SEI.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref29" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1088/0953-8984/21/39/395502"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Giannozzi, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Baroni, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bonini, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Calandra, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Car, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cavazzoni, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ceresoli, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chiarotti, G.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">QUANTUM ESPRESSO: a modular and open-source software project for quantum simulations of materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Giannozzi Paolo; Baroni Stefano; Bonini Nicola; Calandra Matteo; Car Roberto; Cavazzoni Carlo; Ceresoli Davide; Chiarotti Guido L; Cococcioni Matteo; Dabo Ismaila; Dal Corso Andrea; de Gironcoli Stefano; Fabris Stefano; Fratesi Guido; Gebauer Ralph; Gerstmann Uwe; Gougoussis Christos; Kokalj Anton; Lazzeri Michele; Martin-Samos Layla; Marzari Nicola; Mauri Francesco; Mazzarello Riccardo; Paolini Stefano; Pasquarello Alfredo; Paulatto Lorenzo; Sbraccia Carlo; Scandolo Sandro; Sclauzero Gabriele; Seitsonen Ari P; Smogunov Alexander; Umari Paolo; Wentzcovitch Renata M</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of physics.     </div><div class="casAbstract">QUANTUM ESPRESSO is an integrated suite of computer codes for electronic-structure calculations and materials modeling, based on density-functional theory, plane waves, and pseudopotentials (norm-conserving, ultrasoft, and projector-augmented wave).  The acronym ESPRESSO stands for opEn Source Package for Research in Electronic Structure, Simulation, and Optimization.  It is freely available to researchers around the world under the terms of the GNU General Public License.  QUANTUM ESPRESSO builds upon newly-restructured electronic-structure codes that have been developed and tested by some of the original authors of novel electronic-structure algorithms and applied in the last twenty years by some of the leading materials modeling groups worldwide.  Innovation and efficiency are still its main focus, with special attention paid to massively parallel architectures, and a great effort being devoted to user friendliness.  QUANTUM ESPRESSO is evolving towards a distribution of independent and interoperable codes in the spirit of an open-source project, where researchers active in the field of electronic-structure calculations are encouraged to participate in the project by contributing their own codes or by implementing their own ideas into existing codes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref30" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b01132"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goodenough, J.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Theoretical Study of the Structural Evolution of a Na2FeMn(CN)6 Cathode upon Na Intercalation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Penghao; Song, Jie; Wang, Long; Goodenough, John B.; Henkelman, Graeme</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The Prussian Blue analog, NaxFeMn(CN)6, is a potential new cathode material for Na-ion batteries.  During Na intercalation, the dehydrated material exhibits a monoclinic to rhombohedral phase transition, while the hydrated material remains in the monoclinic phase.  With d. functional theory calcns., the phase transition is explained in terms of a competition between Coulomb attraction, Pauli repulsion, and d-π covalent bonding.  The interstitial Na cations have a strong Coulomb attraction to the N anions in the host material, which tend to bend the Mn-N bonds and reduce the vol. of the structure.  The presence of lattice H2O enhances the Pauli repulsion so that the vol. redn. is suppressed.  The calcd. vol. change, as it depends upon the presence of lattice H2O, is consistent with exptl. measurements.  Addnl., a new LiFeMn(CN)6 phase is predicted where MnN6 octahedra decomp. into LiN4 and MnN4 edge-sharing tetrahedra.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref31" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201600747"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Prussian Blue@C Composite as an Ultrahigh-Rate and Long-Life Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode</span>. <i>Adv.                 <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable sodium ion batteries (SIBs) are surfacing as promising candidates for applications in large-scale energy-storage systems.  Prussian blue (PB) and its analogs (PBAs) have been considered as potential cathodes because of their rigid open framework and low-cost synthesis.  Nevertheless, PBAs suffer from inferior rate capability and poor cycling stability resulting from the low electronic cond. and deficiencies in the PBAs framework.  Herein, to understand the vacancy-impacted sodium storage and Na-insertion reaction kinetics, we report on an in-situ synthesized PB@C composite as a high-performance SIB cathode.  Perfectly shaped, nanosized PB cubes were grown directly on carbon chains, assuring fast charge transfer and Na-ion diffusion.  The existence of [Fe(CN)6] vacancies in the PB crystal is found to greatly degrade the electrochem. activity of the FeLS(C) redox couple via first-principles computation.  Superior reaction kinetics are demonstrated for the redox reactions of the FeHS(N) couple, which rely on the partial insertion of Na ions to enhance the electron conduction.  The synergistic effects of the structure and morphol. results in the PB@C composite achieving an unprecedented rate capability and outstanding cycling stability (77.5 mAh g-1 at 90 C, 90 mAh g-1 after 2000 cycles at 20 C with 90% capacity retention).</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref32" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b12620"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Crystallized Na2CoFe(CN)6 with Suppressed Lattice Defects as Superior Cathode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly Crystallized Na2CoFe(CN)6 with Suppressed Lattice Defects as Superior Cathode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xianyong; Wu, Chenghao; Wei, Congxiao; Hu, Ling; Qian, Jiangfeng; Cao, Yuliang; Ai, Xinping; Wang, Jiulin; Yang, Hanxi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue and its analogs have received particular attention as superior cathodes for Na-ion batteries due to their potential 2-Na storage capacity (∼170 mA-h g-1) and low cost.  However, most of the Prussian blue compds. obtained from the conventional synthetic routes contain large amts. of Fe(CN)6 vacancies and coordinated H2O mols., which leads to the collapse of cyano-bridged framework and serious deterioration of their Na-storage ability.  Herein, the authors propose a facile citrate-assisted controlled crystn. method to obtain low-defect Prussian blue lattice with greatly improved Na-storage capacity and cycling stability.  As an example, the as-prepd. Na2CoFe(CN)6 nanocrystals demonstrate a reversible 2-Na storage reaction with a high specific capacity of 150 mA-h g-1 and a ∼ 90% capacity retention over 200 cycles, possibly serving as a low cost and high performance cathode for Na-ion batteries.  In particular, the synthetic strategy described in this work may be extended to other coordination-framework materials for a wide range of energy conversion and storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref33" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b06880"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Low Defect FeFe(CN)6 Framework as Stable Host Material for High Performance Li-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Low cost and high performance Li-ion batteries have been extensively pursued for grid-scale energy storage applications, however, their development has been impeded for a long time due to the lack of qualified cathode materials with not only decent electrochem. performance but also resource abundance and low price.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Non-Prussian Blue Structures and Magnetic Ordering of Na2MnII[MnII(CN)6] and Na2MnII[MnII(CN)6]·2H2O</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kareis, Christopher M.; Lapidus, Saul H.; Her, Jae-Hyuk; Stephens, Peter W.; Miller, Joel S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">134</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The aq. reaction of MnII and NaCN gives the 3-dimensional Prussian blue analog (PBA) Na2Mn[Mn(CN)6]·2H2O (1·H2O), which under careful dehydration forms 1.  1·H2O is monoclinic [P21/n, a 10.66744(32), b 7.60223(23), c 7.40713(22) Å, β 92.4379(28)°], while 1 is rhombohedral [R‾3, a 6.6166(2), c 19.2585(6) Å], and both structures are atypical for PBAs, which are typically fcc.  Most notably, the av. ∠Mn-N-C angles are 165.3(3)° and 142.4(4)° for 1·H2O and 1, resp., which are significantly reduced from linearity.  This is attributed to the ionic nature of high-spin MnII accommodating a reduced ∠Mn-N-C to minimize void space.  Both 1 and 1·H2O magnetically order as ferrimagnets below their ordering temp., Tc, of 58 and 30 K, resp., as detd. from the av. of several independent methods.  1 And 1·H2O are hard magnets with 5 K coercive fields of 15,300 and 850 Oe, and remnant magnetizations of 9075 and 102 emu Oe/mol, resp.  These data along with previous Tc's reported for related materials reveal that Tc increases as the ∠Mn-N-C deviates further from linearity.  Hence, the bent cyanide bridges play a crucial role in the superexchange mechanism by increasing the coupling via shorter MnII···MnII sepns., and perhaps an enhanced overlap.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref37" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1021/ja044959o"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Serena, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kosmas, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fitch, A. X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Interplay between Electrochemistry and Phase Evolution of the P2-type Nax(Fe1/2Mn1/2)O2 Cathode for Use in Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>27</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3150</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3158</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b00943</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D27%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D3150-3158%26journal%3DChem.%2BMater.%26author%3DW.%2BK.%2BPang%26author%3DS.%2BKalluri%26author%3DV.%2BK.%2BPeterson%26author%3DN.%2BSharma%26author%3DJ.%2BKimpton%26author%3DB.%2BJohannessen%26author%3DH.%2BK.%2BLiu%26author%3DS.%2BX.%2BDou%26author%3DZ.%2BGuo%26title%3DInterplay%2Bbetween%2BElectrochemistry%2Band%2BPhase%2BEvolution%2Bof%2Bthe%2BP2-type%2BNax%2528Fe1%252F2Mn1%252F2%2529O2%2BCathode%2Bfor%2BUse%2Bin%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.chemmater.5b00943&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11157&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.chemmater.5b00943&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interplay between Electrochemistry and Phase Evolution of the P2-type Nax(Fe1/2Mn1/2)O2 Cathode for Use in Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pang, Wei Kong; Kalluri, Sujith; Peterson, Vanessa K.; Sharma, Neeraj; Kimpton, Justin; Johannessen, Bernt; Liu, Hua Kun; Dou, Shi Xue; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3150-3158</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are the next-generation in battery technol.; however, their com. development is hampered by electrode performance.  The P2-type Na2/3(Fe1/2Mn1/2)O2 with a hexagonal structure and P63/mmc space group is considered a candidate sodium-ion battery cathode material due to its high capacity (∼190 mAh·g-1) and energy d. (∼520 mWh·g-1), which are comparable to those of the com. LiFePO4 and LiMn2O4 lithium-ion battery cathodes, with previously unexplained poor cycling performance being the major barrier to its com. application.  The operando synchrotron X-ray powder diffraction is used to understand the origins of the capacity fade of the Na2/3(Fe1/2Mn1/2)O2 material during cycling over the relatively wide 1.5-4.2 V (vs. Na) window.  A complex phase-evolution is found, involving transitions from P63/mmc (P2-type at the open-circuit voltage) to P63 (OP4-type when fully charged) to P63/mmc (P2-type at 3.4-2.0 V) to Cmcm (P2-type at 2.0-1.5 V) symmetry structures during the desodiation and sodiation of the Na2/3(Fe1/2Mn1/2)O2 cathode.  The assocd. large cell-vol. changes with the multiple two-phase reactions are likely to be responsible for the poor cycling performance, clearly suggesting a 2.0-4.0 V window of operation as a strategy to improve cycling performance.  It is demonstrated here that the P2-type Na2/3(Fe1/2Mn1/2)O2 cathode is able to deliver ∼25% better cycling performance with the strategic operation window.  This significant improvement in cycling performance implies that by characterizing the phase evolution and reaction mechanisms during battery function these modifications are proposed to the conditions of battery use that improve performance, highlighting the importance of the interplay between structure and electrochem.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref39" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1088/1674-1056/25/1/018210"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, S.-Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Brief Overview of Electrochemical Potential in Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chin. Phys. B</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>25</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">018210</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1088/1674-1056/25/1/018210</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D25%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D018210%26journal%3DChin.%2BPhys.%2BB%26author%3DJ.%2BGao%26author%3DS.-Q.%2BShi%26author%3DH.%2BLi%26title%3DBrief%2BOverview%2Bof%2BElectrochemical%2BPotential%2Bin%2BLithium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1088%252F1674-1056%252F25%252F1%252F018210&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11157&amp;doiOfLink=10.1088%2F1674-1056%2F25%2F1%2F018210&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Brief overview of electrochemical potential in lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gao, Jian; Shi, Si-Qi; Li, Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chinese Physics B</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CPBHAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1674-1056</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">IOP Publishing Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The phys. fundamentals and influences upon electrode materials' open-circuit voltage (OCV) and the spatial distribution of electrochem. potential in the full cell are briefly reviewed.  We hope to illustrate that a better understanding of these scientific problems can help to develop and design high voltage cathodes and interfaces with low Ohmic drop.  OCV is one of the main indexes to evaluate the performance of lithium ion batteries (LIBs), and the enhancement of OCV shows promise as a way to increase the energy d.  Besides, the severe potential drop at the interfaces indicates high resistance there, which is one of the key factors limiting power d.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref40" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2014.12.160"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Self-combustion synthesis of Na3V2(PO4)3 nanoparticles coated with carbon shell as cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim.                 10.1016/j.electacta.2014.12.160</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D155%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D23-28%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DD.%2BJiang%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DG.%2BLi%26author%3DX.%2BLan%26author%3DH.%2BZhong%26author%3DZ.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BJiang%26title%3DSelf-combustion%2Bsynthesis%2Bof%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%2Bnanoparticles%2Bcoated%2Bwith%2Bcarbon%2Bshell%2Bas%2Bcathode%2Bmaterials%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2014.12.160&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11157&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2014.12.160&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-combustion synthesis of Na3V2(PO4)3 nanoparticles coated with carbon shell as cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Hui; Jiang, Danlu; Zhang, Yan; Li, Guopeng; Lan, Xinzheng; Zhong, Honghai; Zhang, Zhongping; Jiang, Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">155</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The real applications of Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode material for sodium batteries have been hindered by low-cost and facile synthesis method.  Herein, we report a facile self-combustion method to synthesize Na3V2(PO4)3 nanoparticles coated with carbon shell (NVP/C).  Used as the cathode, the NVP/C is capable of delivering the initial discharge and charge capacities of 100.72 and 111.3 mA-h/g at the current of 0.1C in a voltage range of 2.5-3.8 V, and the capacity retention of the sample is ∼95% of its initial specific capacity after 50th cycle.  The first-principles simulation results show that the Na ions migration route prefers between two adjacent tetrahedral sites with the vacancy-hopping mechanism in a curved way, with the lowest activation energy of 0.292 eV.  The diffusion coeff. of sodium ions at room temp. was also calcd. to be as high as 2.38 × 10-9 cm2/s.  The results suggest great potential of self-combustion synthesized NVP/C as cathode materials for Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref41" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.04.054"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Glucose-assisted synthesis of Na3V2(PO4)3/C composite as an electrode material for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>J.                 10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.04.054</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D265%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D325-334%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DG.%2BLi%26author%3DD.%2BJiang%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BLan%26author%3DH.%2BZhong%26author%3DY.%2BJiang%26title%3DGlucose-assisted%2Bsynthesis%2Bof%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%252FC%2Bcomposite%2Bas%2Ban%2Belectrode%2Bmaterial%2Bfor%2Bhigh-performance%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2014.04.054&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11157&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2014.04.054&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Glucose-assisted synthesis of Na3V2(PO4)3/C composite as an electrode material for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Guangqiang; Jiang, Danlu; Wang, Hui; Lan, Xinzheng; Zhong, Honghai; Jiang, Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">265</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">325-334</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel electrode material for sodium-ion batteries, Na3V2(PO4)3 with a rhombohedral, Na+ superionic conductor (NASICON)-type structure, was synthesized via a solid-state carbothermal redn. reaction assisted by mechanochem. activation.  Electron microscopy anal. showed that the synthesized Na3V2(PO4)3 particles had an av. size of 300 nm, being coated with a uniform layer of carbon 3 nm in thickness.  As a cathode material, Na3V2(PO4)3/C exhibited an initial specific discharge capacity of 98.17 mA-h/g at 0.1C for potentials ranging from 2.5 to 3.8 V.  This was owing to the V3+/V4+ redox couple, which corresponded to the two-phase transition between Na3V2(PO4)3 and NaV2(PO4)3.  The cathode lost 4.92% of its discharge specific capacity after 50 cycles.  As an anode material, Na3V2(PO4)3/C exhibited an initial specific discharge capacity of 63.2 mA-h/g at 0.1C for potentials ranging from 1.0 to 2.5 V.  This was owing to the V2+/V3+ redox couple, which corresponded to the two-phase transition between Na3V2(PO4)3 and Na4V2(PO4)3.  The anode lost approx. 5.41% of its discharge specific capacity after 50 cycles.  The three-dimensional channel structure of NaV2(PO4)3 and the changes induced in its lattice parameters during the charge/discharge processes were simulated on the basis of d. functional theory.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref42" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1039/c4ta04995k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lotfabad, E.                 10.1002/adfm.201200691</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Slater, Michael D.; Kim, Donghan; Lee, Eungje; Doeff, Marca; Johnson, Christopher S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">23</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The status of ambient temp. sodium ion batteries is reviewed in light of recent developments in anode, electrolyte and cathode materials.  These devices, although early in their stage of development, are promising for large-scale grid storage applications due to the abundance and very low cost of sodium-contg. precursors used to make the components.  The engineering knowledge developed recently for highly successful Li ion batteries can be leveraged to ensure rapid progress in this area, although different electrode materials and electrolytes will be required for dual intercalation systems based on sodium.  In particular, new anode materials need to be identified, since the graphite anode, commonly used in lithium systems, does not intercalate sodium to any appreciable extent.  A wider array of choices is available for cathodes, including high performance layered transition metal oxides and polyanionic compds.  Recent developments in electrodes are encouraging, but a great deal of research is necessary, particularly in new electrolytes, and the understanding of the SEI films.  The engineering modeling calcns. of Na-ion battery energy d. indicate that 210 Wh kg-1 in gravimetric energy is possible for Na-ion batteries compared to existing Li-ion technol. if a cathode capacity of 200 mAh g-1 and a 500 mAh g-1 anode can be discovered with an av. cell potential of 3.3 V.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1021/cr500192f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yabuuchi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahbi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research Development on Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Future outlook of sodium-ion batteries is discussed.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201400173"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jian, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ikuhara, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Atomic Structure and Kinetics of NASICON NaxV2(PO4)3Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>24</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4265</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4272</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.201400173</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atomic Structure and Kinetics of NASICON NaxV2(PO4)3 Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jian, Zelang; Yuan, Chenchen; Han, Wenze; Lu, Xia; Gu, Lin; Xi, Xuekui; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Chen, Wen; Chen, Dongfeng; Ikuhara, Yuichi; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">24</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">27</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4265-4272</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)3 is one of the most important cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries, delivering about two Na extn./insertion from/into the unit structure.  To understand the mechanism of sodium storage, a detailed structure of rhombohedral Na3V2(PO4)3 and its sodium extd. phase of NaV2(PO4)3 are investigated at the at. scale using a variety of advanced techniques.  It is found that two different Na sites (6b, M1 and 18e, M2) with different coordination environments co-exist in Na3V2(PO4)3, whereas only one Na site (6b, M1) exists in NaV2(PO4)3.  When Na is extd. from Na3V2(PO4)3 to form NaV2(PO4)3, Na+ occupying the M2 site (CN = 8) is extd. and the rest of the Na remains at M1 site (CN = 6).  In addn., the Na atoms are not randomly distributed, possibly with an ordered arrangement in M2 sites locally for Na3V2(PO4)3.  Na+ ions at the M1 sites in Na3V2(PO4)3 tend to remain immobilized, suggesting a direct M2-to-M2 conduction pathway.  Only Na occupying the M2 sites can be extd., suggesting about two Na atoms are able to be extd. from the Na3V2(PO4)3 structure.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1039/c5ee01365h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nazar, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Talaie, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duffort, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Smith, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fultz, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structure of the High Voltage Phase of Layered P2-Na<sub>2/3-x</sub>[Mn<sub>1/2</sub>Fe<sub>1/2</sub>]O<sub>2</sub> and the Positive Effect of Ni Substitution on its Stability</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         rightTab-cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-ion mobility in layered Na2FePO4F and olivine Na[Fe,Mn]PO4</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tripathi, R.; Wood, S. M.; Islam, M. S.; Nazar, L. F.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2257-2264</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The Na-ion battery is currently the focus of much research interest due to its cost advantages and the relative abundance of sodium as compared to lithium.  Olivine NaMPO4 (M = Fe, Fe0.5Mn0.5, Mn) and layered Na2FePO4F are interesting materials that have been reported recently as attractive pos. electrodes.  Here, we report their Na-ion conduction behavior and intrinsic defect properties using atomistic simulation methods.  In the olivines, Na ion migration is essentially restricted to the [010] direction along a curved trajectory, similar to that of LiMPO4, but with a lower migration energy (0.3 eV).  However, Na/M antisite defects are also predicted to have a lower formation energy: the higher probability of tunnel occupation with a relatively immobile M2+ cation - along with a greater vol. change on redox cycling - contributes to the poor electrochem. performance of the Na-olivine.  Na+ ion conduction in Na2FePO4F is predicted to be two-dimensional (2D) in the interlayer plane with a similar low activation energy.  The antisite formation energy is slightly higher; furthermore, antisite occupation would not be predicted to impede transport significantly owing to the 2D pathway.  This factor, along with the much lower vol. change on redox cycling, is undoubtedly responsible for the better electrochem. performance of the layered structure.  Where vol. change and structural effects do not incur impediments, Na-ion materials may present significant advantages over their Li counterparts.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1038/nchem.2923"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Maitra, U.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">House, R.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The search for improved energy-storage materials has revealed Li- and Na-rich intercalation compds. as promising high-capacity cathodes.  They exhibit capacities in excess of what would be expected from alkali-ion removal/reinsertion and charge compensation by transition-metal (TM) ions.  The addnl. capacity is provided through charge compensation by oxygen redox chem. and some oxygen loss.  It has been reported previously that oxygen redox occurs in O 2p orbitals that interact with alkali ions in the TM and alkali-ion layers (i.e., oxygen redox occurs in compds. contg. Li+-O(2p)-Li+ interactions).  Na2/3[Mg0.28Mn0.72]O2 exhibits an excess capacity and here we show that this is caused by oxygen redox, even though Mg2+ resides in the TM layers rather than alkali-metal (AM) ions, which demonstrates that excess AM ions are not required to activate oxygen redox.  We also show that, unlike the alkali-rich compds., Na2/3[Mg0.28Mn0.72]O2 does not lose oxygen.  The extn. of alkali ions from the alkali and TM layers in the alkali-rich compds. results in severely underbonded oxygen, which promotes oxygen loss, whereas Mg2+ remains in Na2/3[Mg0.28Mn0.72]O2, which stabilizes oxygen.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702619"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Prussian Blue Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries and Other Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Non-lithium energy storage devices, esp. sodium ion batteries, are drawing attention due to insufficient and uneven distribution of lithium resources.  Prussian blue and its analogs (Prussian blue analogs [PBAs]), or hexacyanoferrates, are well-known since the 18th century and have been used for hydrogen storage, cancer therapy, biosensing, seawater desalination, and sewage treatment.  Owing to their unique features, PBAs are receiving increasing interest in the field of energy storage, such as their high theor. specific capacity, ease of synthesis, as well as low cost.  In this review, a general summary and evaluation of the applications of PBAs for rechargeable batteries are given.  After a brief review of the history of PBAs, their crystal structure, nomenclature, synthesis, and working principle in rechargeable batteries are discussed.  Then, previous works classified based on the combination of insertion cations and transition metals are analyzed comprehensively.  The review includes an outlook toward the further development of PBAs in electrochem. energy storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b04151"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Preparation of Prussian Blue Submicron Particles with a Pore Structure by Two-Step Optimization for Na-Ion Battery Cathodes</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Traditional Prussian blue (Fe4[Fe(CN)6]3) synthesized by simple rapid pptn. shows poor electrochem. performance because of the presence of vacancies occupied by coordinated water. Surprisingly, the electrode shows an initial discharge capacity of 115 mA h g-1 and a Coulombic efficiency of approx. 100% with capacity retention of 96% after 150 cycles.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Designing Prussian blue with optimally exposed crystal planes and confining it in a conductive matrix are crit. issues for improving its sodium storage performance, and will result in much improved sodium ion adsorption and diffusion, together with improved electron mobility.  Here, we firstly illustrate through DFT simulations that the {100} lattice planes and [100] direction of the KxFeFe(CN)6 crystal are the preferred occupation sites and diffusion route for sodium ions.  In addn., through coupling with RGO, KxFeFe(CN)6 electrodes exhibit better electronic cond.  Accordingly, {100} plane-capped cubic K0.33FeFe(CN)6 wrapped in RGO was fabricated using a facile CTAB-assisted method.  Due to the highly robust framework, higher sp. surface area, greatly reduced no. of lattice water defects and conductive RGO coating, K0.33FeFe(CN)6/RGO exhibits superior electrochem. performance in sodium-ion batteries.  As a cathode, the RGO-coated K0.33FeFe(CN)6 yields an initial discharge-charge capacity of 160 mA h g-1 at a rate of 0.5C, and an excellent capacity retention of 92.2% at 0.5C and 90.1% at 10C after 1000 and 500 cycles.  Furthermore, x-ray diffraction, DFT simulation, XANES and EXAFS verified that the structural changes during the Na-ion insertion-extn. processes are highly reversible.  All these results suggest that {100} plane-capped K0.33FeFe(CN)6/RGO has excellent potential as a cathode for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref26" class="rightTabRefNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit26" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-014-0588-7"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">You, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nam, K.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.-G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium Iron Hexacyanoferrate With High Na Content as a Na-Rich Cathode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nano Res.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">117</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">128</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

The solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) is a protecting layer formed on the neg. electrode of Li-ion batteries as a result of electrolyte decompn., mainly during the 1st cycle.  Battery performance, irreversible charge loss, rate capability, cyclability, exfoliation of graphite and safety are highly dependent on the quality of the SEI.  Therefore, understanding the actual nature and compn. of SEI is of prime interest.  If the chem. of the SEI formation and the manner in which each component affects battery performance are understood, SEI could be tuned to improve battery performance.  In this paper key points related to the nature, formation, and features of the SEI formed on carbon neg. electrodes are discussed.  SEI was analyzed by various anal. techniques amongst which FTIR and XPS are most widely used.  FTIR and XPS data of SEI and its components as published by many research groups are compiled in tables for getting a global picture of what is known about the SEI.  This article shall serve as a handy ref. as well as a starting point for research related to SEI.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1088/0953-8984/21/39/395502"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Giannozzi, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Baroni, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bonini, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Calandra, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Car, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cavazzoni, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ceresoli, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chiarotti, G.     </div><div class="casAbstract">QUANTUM ESPRESSO is an integrated suite of computer codes for electronic-structure calculations and materials modeling, based on density-functional theory, plane waves, and pseudopotentials (norm-conserving, ultrasoft, and projector-augmented wave).  The acronym ESPRESSO stands for opEn Source Package for Research in Electronic Structure, Simulation, and Optimization.  It is freely available to researchers around the world under the terms of the GNU General Public License.  QUANTUM ESPRESSO builds upon newly-restructured electronic-structure codes that have been developed and tested by some of the original authors of novel electronic-structure algorithms and applied in the last twenty years by some of the leading materials modeling groups worldwide.  Innovation and efficiency are still its main focus, with special attention paid to massively parallel architectures, and a great effort being devoted to user friendliness.  QUANTUM ESPRESSO is evolving towards a distribution of independent and interoperable codes in the spirit of an open-source project, where researchers active in the field of electronic-structure calculations are encouraged to participate in the project by contributing their own codes or by implementing their own ideas into existing codes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b01132"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goodenough, J.
