        </div><div class="casAbstract">The Prussian Blue analog, NaxFeMn(CN)6, is a potential new cathode material for Na-ion batteries.  During Na intercalation, the dehydrated material exhibits a monoclinic to rhombohedral phase transition, while the hydrated material remains in the monoclinic phase.  With d. functional theory calcns., the phase transition is explained in terms of a competition between Coulomb attraction, Pauli repulsion, and d-π covalent bonding.  The interstitial Na cations have a strong Coulomb attraction to the N anions in the host material, which tend to bend the Mn-N bonds and reduce the vol. of the structure.  The presence of lattice H2O enhances the Pauli repulsion so that the vol. redn. is suppressed.  The calcd. vol. change, as it depends upon the presence of lattice H2O, is consistent with exptl. measurements.  Addnl., a new LiFeMn(CN)6 phase is predicted where MnN6 octahedra decomp. into LiN4 and MnN4 edge-sharing tetrahedra.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref31" class="rightTabRefNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit31" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201600747"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Prussian Blue@C Composite as an Ultrahigh-Rate and Long-Life Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode</span>. <i>Adv. Prussian blue (PB) and its analogs (PBAs) have been considered as potential cathodes because of their rigid open framework and low-cost synthesis.  Nevertheless, PBAs suffer from inferior rate capability and poor cycling stability resulting from the low electronic cond. and deficiencies in the PBAs framework.  Herein, to understand the vacancy-impacted sodium storage and Na-insertion reaction kinetics, we report on an in-situ synthesized PB@C composite as a high-performance SIB cathode.  Perfectly shaped, nanosized PB cubes were grown directly on carbon chains, assuring fast charge transfer and Na-ion diffusion.  The existence of [Fe(CN)6] vacancies in the PB crystal is found to greatly degrade the electrochem. activity of the FeLS(C) redox couple via first-principles computation.  Superior reaction kinetics are demonstrated for the redox reactions of the FeHS(N) couple, which rely on the partial insertion of Na ions to enhance the electron conduction.  The synergistic effects of the structure and morphol. results in the PB@C composite achieving an unprecedented rate capability and outstanding cycling stability (77.5 mAh g-1 at 90 C, 90 mAh g-1 after 2000 cycles at 20 C with 90% capacity retention).</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b12620"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Crystallized Na2CoFe(CN)6 with Suppressed Lattice Defects as Superior Cathode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.     <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2246-2254</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The aq. reaction of MnII and NaCN gives the 3-dimensional Prussian blue analog (PBA) Na2Mn[Mn(CN)6]·2H2O (1·H2O), which under careful dehydration forms 1.  1·H2O is monoclinic [P21/n, a 10.66744(32), b 7.60223(23), c 7.40713(22) Å, β 92.4379(28)°], while 1 is rhombohedral [R‾3, a 6.6166(2), c 19.2585(6) Å], and both structures are atypical for PBAs, which are typically fcc.  Most notably, the av. ∠Mn-N-C angles are 165.3(3)° and 142.4(4)° for 1·H2O and 1, resp., which are significantly reduced from linearity.  This is attributed to the ionic nature of high-spin MnII accommodating a reduced ∠Mn-N-C to minimize void space.  Both 1 and 1·H2O magnetically order as ferrimagnets below their ordering temp., Tc, of 58 and 30 K, resp., as detd. from the av. of several independent methods.  1 And 1·H2O are hard magnets with 5 K coercive fields of 15,300 and 850 Oe, and remnant magnetizations of 9075 and 102 emu Oe/mol, resp.  These data along with previous Tc's reported for related materials reveal that Tc increases as the ∠Mn-N-C deviates further from linearity.  Hence, the bent cyanide bridges play a crucial role in the superexchange mechanism by increasing the coupling via shorter MnII···MnII sepns., and perhaps an enhanced overlap.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref37" class="rightTabRefNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit37" data-doi="10.1021/ja044959o"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Serena, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kosmas, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fitch, A. N.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Zero Thermal Expansion in a Prussian Blue Analogue</span>. <i>J. Am. Chem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2004</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>126</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">15390</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">15391</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/ja044959o</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b00943"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, W. K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kalluri, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peterson, V. K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sharma, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kimpton, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Johannessen, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H. K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S. X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Interplay between Electrochemistry and Phase Evolution of the P2-type Nax(Fe1/2Mn1/2)O2 Cathode for Use in Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>27</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3150</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3158</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b00943</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interplay between Electrochemistry and Phase Evolution of the P2-type Nax(Fe1/2Mn1/2)O2 Cathode for Use in Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pang, Wei Kong; Kalluri, Sujith; Peterson, Vanessa K.; Sharma, Neeraj; Kimpton, Justin; Johannessen, Bernt; Liu, Hua Kun; Dou, Shi Xue; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3150-3158</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are the next-generation in battery technol.; however, their com. development is hampered by electrode performance.  The P2-type Na2/3(Fe1/2Mn1/2)O2 with a hexagonal structure and P63/mmc space group is considered a candidate sodium-ion battery cathode material due to its high capacity (∼190 mAh·g-1) and energy d. (∼520 mWh·g-1), which are comparable to those of the com. LiFePO4 and LiMn2O4 lithium-ion battery cathodes, with previously unexplained poor cycling performance being the major barrier to its com. application.  The operando synchrotron X-ray powder diffraction is used to understand the origins of the capacity fade of the Na2/3(Fe1/2Mn1/2)O2 material during cycling over the relatively wide 1.5-4.2 V (vs. Na) window.  A complex phase-evolution is found, involving transitions from P63/mmc (P2-type at the open-circuit voltage) to P63 (OP4-type when fully charged) to P63/mmc (P2-type at 3.4-2.0 V) to Cmcm (P2-type at 2.0-1.5 V) symmetry structures during the desodiation and sodiation of the Na2/3(Fe1/2Mn1/2)O2 cathode.  The assocd. large cell-vol. changes with the multiple two-phase reactions are likely to be responsible for the poor cycling performance, clearly suggesting a 2.0-4.0 V window of operation as a strategy to improve cycling performance.  It is demonstrated here that the P2-type Na2/3(Fe1/2Mn1/2)O2 cathode is able to deliver ∼25% better cycling performance with the strategic operation window.  This significant improvement in cycling performance implies that by characterizing the phase evolution and reaction mechanisms during battery function these modifications are proposed to the conditions of battery use that improve performance, highlighting the importance of the interplay between structure and electrochem.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref39" class="rightTabRefNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit39" data-doi="10.1088/1674-1056/25/1/018210"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, S.-Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Brief Overview of Electrochemical Potential in Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chin. Phys. B</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>25</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">018210</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1088/1674-1056/25/1/018210</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Brief overview of electrochemical potential in lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gao, Jian; Shi, Si-Qi; Li, Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chinese Physics B</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">018210/1-018210/24</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CPBHAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1674-1056</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">IOP Publishing Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The phys. fundamentals and influences upon electrode materials' open-circuit voltage (OCV) and the spatial distribution of electrochem. potential in the full cell are briefly reviewed.  We hope to illustrate that a better understanding of these scientific problems can help to develop and design high voltage cathodes and interfaces with low Ohmic drop.  OCV is one of the main indexes to evaluate the performance of lithium ion batteries (LIBs), and the enhancement of OCV shows promise as a way to increase the energy d.  Besides, the severe potential drop at the interfaces indicates high resistance there, which is one of the key factors limiting power d.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref40" class="rightTabRefNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit40" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2014.12.160"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Self-combustion synthesis of Na3V2(PO4)3 nanoparticles coated with carbon shell as cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim. Acta</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>155</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">23</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">28</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2014.12.160</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-combustion synthesis of Na3V2(PO4)3 nanoparticles coated with carbon shell as cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Hui; Jiang, Danlu; Zhang, Yan; Li, Guopeng; Lan, Xinzheng; Zhong, Honghai; Zhang, Zhongping; Jiang, Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">155</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">23-28</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The real applications of Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode material for sodium batteries have been hindered by low-cost and facile synthesis method.  Herein, we report a facile self-combustion method to synthesize Na3V2(PO4)3 nanoparticles coated with carbon shell (NVP/C).  Used as the cathode, the NVP/C is capable of delivering the initial discharge and charge capacities of 100.72 and 111.3 mA-h/g at the current of 0.1C in a voltage range of 2.5-3.8 V, and the capacity retention of the sample is ∼95% of its initial specific capacity after 50th cycle.  The first-principles simulation results show that the Na ions migration route prefers between two adjacent tetrahedral sites with the vacancy-hopping mechanism in a curved way, with the lowest activation energy of 0.292 eV.  The diffusion coeff. of sodium ions at room temp. was also calcd. to be as high as 2.38 × 10-9 cm2/s.  The results suggest great potential of self-combustion synthesized NVP/C as cathode materials for Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref41" class="rightTabRefNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.04.054"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Glucose-assisted synthesis of Na3V2(PO4)3/C composite as an electrode material for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>J. Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>265</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">325</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">334</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.04.054</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Glucose-assisted synthesis of Na3V2(PO4)3/C composite as an electrode material for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Guangqiang; Jiang, Danlu; Wang, Hui; Lan, Xinzheng; Zhong, Honghai; Jiang, Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">265</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">325-334</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel electrode material for sodium-ion batteries, Na3V2(PO4)3 with a rhombohedral, Na+ superionic conductor (NASICON)-type structure, was synthesized via a solid-state carbothermal redn. reaction assisted by mechanochem. activation.  Electron microscopy anal. showed that the synthesized Na3V2(PO4)3 particles had an av. size of 300 nm, being coated with a uniform layer of carbon 3 nm in thickness.  As a cathode material, Na3V2(PO4)3/C exhibited an initial specific discharge capacity of 98.17 mA-h/g at 0.1C for potentials ranging from 2.5 to 3.8 V.  This was owing to the V3+/V4+ redox couple, which corresponded to the two-phase transition between Na3V2(PO4)3 and NaV2(PO4)3.  The cathode lost 4.92% of its discharge specific capacity after 50 cycles.  As an anode material, Na3V2(PO4)3/C exhibited an initial specific discharge capacity of 63.2 mA-h/g at 0.1C for potentials ranging from 1.0 to 2.5 V.  This was owing to the V2+/V3+ redox couple, which corresponded to the two-phase transition between Na3V2(PO4)3 and Na4V2(PO4)3.  The anode lost approx. 5.41% of its discharge specific capacity after 50 cycles.  The three-dimensional channel structure of NaV2(PO4)3 and the changes induced in its lattice parameters during the charge/discharge processes were simulated on the basis of d. functional theory.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref42" class="rightTabRefNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit42" data-doi="10.1039/c4ta04995k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lotfabad, E. M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kalisvaart, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kohandehghan, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Karpuzov, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mitlin, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Origin of non-SEI related coulombic efficiency loss in carbons tested against Na and Li</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">19685</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">19695</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c4ta04995k</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i7">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.8b11157" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.8b11157</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">TEM, XPS, EIS, and CPMD simulation results of NMHCF and NMHCF/RGO (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11157/suppl_file/am8b11157_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b11157/suppl_file/am8b11157_si_001.pdf">am8b11157_si_001.pdf (1.53 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

        <script nonce="931888f9eef754b8-SJC">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="931888f9eef754b8-SJC">
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {
    const modalContainer = document.querySelector('.my-main-container');

    // Function to show the modal
    function showModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'flex';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'block';
    }

    // Function to hide the modal when the close button is clicked
    function hideModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'none';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'none';
    }

    // Hide the modal initially
    hideModal();

    // Function to handle clicks outside the modal
    function handleClickOutside(event) {
        // const modalContainer = document.querySelector(".my-main-container");
        // Check if the click target is not a child of the modal container
        if (!modalContainer.contains(event.target)) {
            hideModal();
        }
    }

    // Add a click event listener to the close button
    document
        .querySelector('.close-button')
        .addEventListener('click', hideModal);

    // Add a click event listener to the document to handle clicks outside the modal
    document.addEventListener('click', handleClickOutside);

    const screenHeight = window.innerHeight;
    function updateModalPosition() {
        const scrollY = window.scrollY;
        // console.log("scrollY= " + scrollY);
        // modalContainer.style.top = `${50 + scrollY}px`;
        modalContainer.style.top = `${scrollY + screenHeight / 2}px`;
        // console.log("new top= " + modalContainer.style.top);
    }

    // Update the modal position when the user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', updateModalPosition);

    // Initialize the modal position
    updateModalPosition();

    //---Cookie---
    // Function to set the cookie with a given name, value, and expiration time in days
    function setCookie(name, value, days) {
        var expires = '';
        if (days) {
            var date = new Date();
            date.setTime(date.getTime() + days * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000);
            expires = '; expires=' + date.toUTCString();
            console.log(expires + 'this is expires dateUTC');
        }
        document.cookie = name + '=' + (value || '') + expires + '; path=/';
        // console.log("document.cookie is: " + document.cookie);
    }

    if (!document.cookie.includes('modalAd')) {
        // Show Modal
        showModal();

        // Set the cookie with the name "modalAd", value "true", and expiration of 3 day
        setCookie('modalAd', 'true', 3);
    } else {
        hideModal();
    }
});

</script>
<link rel="stylesheet" type="text/css" href="/pb-assets/smartgroup_ads/Modal-LeadGen-1691422642793.css">
            
        </div>

        <span class="system-message-date">Thursday, April 17, 2025</span>
        <p>Please be aware that pubs.acs.org is undergoing maintenance from Saturday February 1 to Monday Febraury 3, that may have an impact on your experience. During this time, you may not be able to access certain features like login, purchasing single articles, saving searches or running existing saved searches, modifying your e-Alert preferences, or accessing Librarian administrative functions. <script nonce="931888f9eef754b8-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

      var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage =
          "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

      function init() {
        setTimeout(function () {
          var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
          if (cookieExist) {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
            return false;
          } else {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
            gdprMessage();
          }
          //Events
          $("#closebtn").on("click", hideForm);

          //Handle submit
          $("#gdpr-message-btn").on("click", function (event) {
            handleClick();
          });

          // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
          // $(document).click(function(event) {
          // 	event.stopPropagation();
          //   console.log(event.target);
          //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
          //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
          //     $(this).off();

            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            hideForm();
          });

      function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();
      }

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
      }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;
          $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
      }

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

    $(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
  </script>
</p>

        <script nonce="931888f9eef754b8-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>

            if ( status == 'success' ) {
